data-v-b3fd67f8><div class="item" data-v-b3fd67f8><div class="indicator" data-v-b3fd67f8></div><a class="VPLink link vp-external-link-icon link" href="https://jesse.trade/strategies/" target="_blank" Roadmap</p><!--]--></a><!----></div><!----></div><!--]--></div></section></div><!--]--><!--[--><!--]--></nav></aside><div class="VPContent has-sidebar" id="VPContent" data-v-5d98c3a5 data-v-1428d186><div class="VPDoc has-sidebar has-aside" data-v-1428d186 data-v-39a288b8><!--[--><!--]--><div class="container" data-v-39a288b8><div class="aside" data-v-39a288b8><div class="aside-curtain" data-v-39a288b8></div><div class="aside-container" data-v-39a288b8><div class="aside-content" data-v-39a288b8><div class="VPDocAside" data-v-39a288b8 data-v-3f215769><!--[--><!--]--><!--[--><!--]--><nav aria-labelledby="doc-outline-aria-label" class="VPDocAsideOutline" data-v-3f215769 data-v-a5bbad30><div class="content" data-v-a5bbad30><div class="outline-marker" data-v-a5bbad30></div><div aria-level="2" class="outline-title" id="doc-outline-aria-label" role="heading" data-v-a5bbad30>On this page</div><ul class="VPDocOutlineItem root" data-v-a5bbad30 data-v-b933a997><!--[--><!--]--></ul></div></nav><!--[--><!--]--><div class="spacer" data-v-3f215769></div><!--[--><!--]--><!----><!--[--><!--]--><!--[--><!--]--></div></div></div></div><div class="content" data-v-39a288b8><div class="content-container" data-v-39a288b8><!--[--><!--]--><main class="main" data-v-39a288b8><div style="position:relative;" class="vp-doc _docs_indicators_reference" data-v-39a288b8><div><h1 id="indicators-reference" tabindex="-1">Indicators Reference <a class="header-anchor" href="#indicators-reference" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;Indicators Reference&quot;">​</a></h1><p>Most indicators have a <code>sequential=False</code> parameter. When set to <code>True</code>, it returns an array of values; which is helpful if you&#39;re doing research in <a href="/docs/research/jupyter" title="Jupyter Notebooks">Jupyter Notebooks</a>.</p><p>When developing strategies however, you probably want to keep it as <code>False</code> to return only the indicator value for current trading candle.</p><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">@cached</p><p>The @cached decorator can increase performance a lot if applied to indicators - especially those called a lot in your strategy. <a href='https://docs.jesse.trade/docs/strategies/api#cached' rel='noreferrer' target='_blank' title='See here'>See here</a>.</p></div><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">Performance and sequential</p><p>With <code>sequential=False</code> the indicators will slice the candle array behind the scene to the warmup_candles_num you defined. That doesn&#39;t happen if you use <code>sequential=True</code>, as Jesse doesn&#39;t know how much lookback you need from your sequential indicator. To keep things fast you should slice the candles yourself before passing them to a indicator function to avoid unnecessary computation time: <code>self.candles[-60:]</code> - change the number accordingly.</p></div><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">matype</p><p>In few indicators you can set a moving average type. Your choices are:</p><ul><li><code>0</code>: sma (simple)</li><li><code>1</code>: ema (exponential)</li><li><code>2</code>: wma (weighted)</li><li><code>3</code>: dema (double exponential)</li><li><code>4</code>: tema (triple exponential)</li><li><code>5</code>: trima (triangular)</li><li><code>6</code>: kama (Kaufman adaptive)</li><li><code>7</code>: mama (Mesa adaptive)</li><li><code>8</code>: T3 (triple exponential T3)</li><li><code>9</code>: fwma (Fibonacci&#39;s Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>10</code>: hma (Hull Moving Average)</li><li><code>11</code>: linearreg (Linear Regression)</li><li><code>12</code>: wilders (Wilders Smoothing)</li><li><code>13</code>: sinwma (Sine Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>14</code>: supersmoother (Super Smoother Filter 2pole Butterworth)</li><li><code>15</code>: supersmoother_3_pole(Super Smoother Filter 3pole Butterworth)</li><li><code>16</code>: gauss (Gaussian Filter)</li><li><code>17</code>: high_pass (1-pole High Pass Filter by John F. Ehlers)</li><li><code>18</code>: high_pass_2_pole (2-pole High Pass Filter by John F. Ehlers)</li><li><code>19</code>: ht_trendline (Hilbert Transform - Instantaneous Trendline)</li><li><code>20</code>: jma (Jurik Moving Average)</li><li><code>21</code>: reflex (Reflex indicator by John F. Ehlers)</li><li><code>22</code>: trendflex (Trendflex indicator by John F. Ehlers)</li><li><code>23</code>: smma (Smoothed Moving Average)</li><li><code>24</code>: vwma (Volume Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>25</code>: pwma (Pascals Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>26</code>: swma (Symmetric Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>27</code>: alma (Arnaud Legoux Moving Average)</li><li><code>28</code>: hwma (Holt-Winter Moving Average)</li><li><code>29</code>: vwap (Volume weighted average price)</li><li><code>30</code>: nma (Natural Moving Average)</li><li><code>31</code>: edcf (Ehlers Distance Coefficient Filter)</li><li><code>32</code>: mwdx (MWDX Average)</li><li><code>33</code>: maaq (Moving Average Adaptive Q)</li><li><code>34</code>: srwma (Square Root Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>35</code>: sqwma (Square Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>36</code>: vpwma (Variable Power Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>37</code>: cwma (Cubed Weighted Moving Average)</li><li><code>38</code>: jsa (Jsa Moving Average)</li><li><code>39</code>: epma (End Point Moving Average)</li></ul></div><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">devtype</p><p>In few indicators you can set a deviation type. Your choices are:</p><ul><li><code>0</code>: standard deviation</li><li><code>1</code>: mean absolute deviation</li><li><code>2</code>: median absolute deviation</li></ul></div><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">source_type</p><p>In some indicators you can set the source type. Your choices are:</p><ul><li><code>&quot;close&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;high&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;low&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;open&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;volume&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;hl2&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;hlc3&quot;</code></li><li><code>&quot;ohlc4&quot;</code></li></ul></div><h2 id="acosc" tabindex="-1">acosc <a class="header-anchor" href="#acosc" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;acosc&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">acosc(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> AC</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Acceleration/Deceleration Oscillator (AC)</strong> is a technical indicator that measures the acceleration or deceleration of a security&#39;s price momentum by subtracting a 5-period simple moving average from a 34-period simple moving average of its price, providing signals for potential changes in trend direction.</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>AC(osc, change)</p><h2 id="ad" tabindex="-1">ad <a class="header-anchor" href="#ad" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;ad&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">ad(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Chaikin A/D Line</strong> is an accumulation/distribution indicator that calculates the sum of money flows based on price movements and volume to identify trends and potential reversals in the price action of a stock.</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="adosc" tabindex="-1">adosc <a class="header-anchor" href="#adosc" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;adosc&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">adosc(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">fast_period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">3</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">slow_period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">10</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Chaikin A/D Oscillator</strong> is a momentum oscillator derived from the Chaikin Accumulation/Distribution Line, indicating the momentum of accumulation or distribution within a security by measuring the difference between its short-term and long-term accumulation/distribution values.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>fast_period</code>: int - default=3</li><li><code>slow_period</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="adx" tabindex="-1">adx <a class="header-anchor" href="#adx" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;adx&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">adx(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">14</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Average Directional Movement Index (ADX)</strong> is a technical indicator used to quantify the strength of a trend in a security, irrespective of its direction, by measuring the magnitude of price movements over a specified time period.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="adxr" tabindex="-1">adxr <a class="header-anchor" href="#adxr" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;adxr&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">adxr(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">14</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Average Directional Movement Index Rating (ADXR)</strong> is a variation of the ADX indicator that calculates the average of the current ADX value and a previous ADX value to provide a smoothed indication of the trend strength over time.</p><p><strong>Author:</strong> KivancOzbilgic</p><p><strong>Credits:</strong> <a href="https://www.tradingview.com/script/9f5zDi3r/" np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="alligator" tabindex="-1">alligator <a class="header-anchor" href="#alligator" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;alligator&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" AG</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Alligator</strong> is a technical analysis tool composed of three smoothed moving averages with different periods, representing the balance between trend-following and range-bound market conditions, helping traders identify potential trends and trade signals.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: lips)</p><h2 id="alma" tabindex="-1">alma <a class="header-anchor" href="#alma" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;alma&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy <strong>Arnaud Legoux Moving Average (ALMA)</strong> is a unique moving average that adjusts its sensitivity based on market volatility, aiming to reduce lag and provide smoother trend signals by incorporating a variable smoothing factor calculated from the Gaussian distribution.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: BandPass</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Bandpass</strong> function isolates specific frequency ranges within price data by applying a bandpass filter. It calculates signals useful for technical analysis and trading strategies by normalizing the filtered data and comparing it to a trigger signal.</p><p>#filter</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>bandwidth</code>: float - default=0.3</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>BandPass(bp, bp_normalized, signal, trigger)</p><h2 id="bollinger-bands" tabindex="-1">bollinger_bands <a class="header-anchor" href="#bollinger-bands" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;bollinger\_bands&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">bollinger_bands(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> BollingerBands</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Bollinger Bands</strong> are a technical analysis tool consisting of a middle band being a simple moving average (SMA) and upper and lower bands representing a specified number of standard deviations from the SMA, used to measure volatility and identify potential overbought or oversold conditions in a security&#39;s price.</p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>devup</code>: float - default=2</li><li><code>devdn</code>: float - default=2</li><li><code>matype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>devtype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>BollingerBands(upperband, middleband, lowerband)</p><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">devtype</p><p>The <code>devtype</code> argument determines the type of deviation to use. If <code>devtype</code> is 0, standard deviation is used. If <code>devtype</code> is 1, mean absolute deviation is used. If <code>devtype</code> is 2, median absolute deviation is used.</p></div><h2 id="bollinger-bands-width" tabindex="-1">bollinger_bands_width <a class="header-anchor" href="#bollinger-bands-width" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;bollinger\_bands\_width&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span moving average, providing insights into the volatility of a security and potential trading opportunities based on changes in volatility levels.</p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>mult</code>: float - default=2</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="bop" tabindex="-1">bop <a class="header-anchor" href="#bop" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;bop&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" <strong>Coppock Curve</strong> is a momentum indicator used in technical analysis to identify long-term buying opportunities in the stock market by calculating the summation of two weighted moving averages of the rate of change for two different time periods.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>wma_period</code>: int - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="cci" tabindex="-1">cci <a &quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, squential: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">bool</span><span by placing stops at a distance from the current price proportional to recent price fluctuations.</p><p>#exit</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>CKSP(long, short)</p><h2 id="chande" tabindex="-1">chande <a class="header-anchor" href="#chande" aria-label="Permalink to <strong>Chande Momentum Oscillator</strong> measures the momentum of a security by calculating the difference between the sum of recent gains and losses over a specified period, providing insights into overbought and oversold conditions and potential trend reversals.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - CC</span></span></code></pre></div><p>John Ehlers&#39; <strong>Correlation Cycle, Correlation Angle, and Market State</strong> are components of a market analysis framework aimed at identifying cyclical patterns and trend directions in financial markets. The Correlation Cycle measures the cyclic behavior of market data, the Correlation Angle quantifies the phase angle of market cycles, and the Market State evaluates the current state of the market, aiding traders in making informed decisions based on cyclical and trend characteristics.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - A value close to 1 indicates the values tend to move in the same direction, while a value close to -1 indicates they tend to move in opposite directions. A value near 0 suggests little correlation.</p><h1 id="trend" tabindex="-1">trend <a class="header-anchor" href="#trend" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;trend&quot;">​</a></h1><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="cvi" tabindex="-1">cvi <a class="header-anchor" href="#cvi" aria-label="Permalink to <strong>Cubed Weighted Moving Average</strong> is a variant of the Weighted Moving Average that assigns higher weights to recent data points cubically, resulting in more emphasis on recent price DamianiVolatmeter</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Damiani Volatmeter</strong> is a technical indicator used to gauge market volatility by comparing the difference between the high and low prices with a reference level over a specified period, providing insights into potential changes in market volatility and helping traders adjust their strategies accordingly.</p><p><strong>Author:</strong> RicardoSantos</p><p><strong>Credits:</strong> <a href="https://www.tradingview.com/v/rYWBBk3a/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer">https://www.tradingview.com/v/rYWBBk3a/</a></p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>vis_atr</code>: int - style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Ehlers Simple Decycler</strong> is a technical indicator developed by John Ehlers that aims to filter out high-frequency noise from price data while preserving the underlying trend. It achieves this by applying a low-pass filter to the price series, emphasizing longer-term price movements and reducing short-term fluctuations.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>hp_period</code>: int - default=125</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="dec-osc" tabindex="-1">dec_osc <a class="header-anchor" href="#dec-osc" aria-label="Permalink to <strong>Ehlers Decycler Oscillator</strong> seeks to filter out short-term price fluctuations and highlight longer-term trends in the market. It accomplishes this by applying a high-pass filter to the price data, effectively removing high-frequency noise and emphasizing the underlying cyclical components of the price series.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>hp_period</code>: int - default=125</li><li><code>k</code>: float - default=1</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="dema" tabindex="-1">dema <a class="header-anchor" href="#dema" <strong>Double Exponential Moving Average (DEMA)</strong> is a type of moving average that applies two exponential smoothing techniques to the price data, resulting in a smoother and more responsive indicator compared to traditional moving averages. It aims to reduce lag and provide quicker signals by placing more weight on recent price data while still maintaining a stable average.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=30</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="devstop" tabindex="-1">devstop <a behavior.</p><p>#exit</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>mult</code>: float - default=0</li><li><code>devtype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="di" tabindex="-1">di <a class="header-anchor" href="#di" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;di&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">di(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span DI</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Directional Indicator</strong> is a technical analysis tool that measures the strength and direction of a trend in a financial market. It consists of two components: The positive Directional Indicator (+DI) and the negative Directional Indicator (-DI) - quantifying the strength of the price movements.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>DI(plus, minus)</p><h2 id="dm" tabindex="-1">dm <a class="header-anchor" href="#dm" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;dm&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">dm(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">14</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> DM</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Directional Movement</strong> is a concept in technical analysis that quantifies the strength and direction of price movements in a financial market. It&#39;s often used in conjunction with the Directional Indicator (DI) to assess the strength of trends. Directional Movement is typically calculated using the True Range (TR) and measures the magnitude of price movements without considering direction. By comparing upward and downward price movements, traders can determine the prevailing direction and strength of a trend.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>DM(plus, minus)</p><h2 id="donchian" tabindex="-1">donchian <a class="header-anchor" href="#donchian" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;donchian&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">donchian(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">20</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> DonchianChannel</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Donchian Channels</strong> are used to identify potential breakout and breakdown levels, as well as to gauge the overall volatility of a market. Traders often use these channels to establish entry and exit points for their trades, with breakouts above the upper channel signaling potential buy opportunities and breakdowns below the lower channel indicating potential sell opportunities.</p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>DonchianChannel(upperband, middleband, lowerband)</p><h2 id="dpo" tabindex="-1">dpo <a class="header-anchor" href="#dpo" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;dpo&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">dpo(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">5</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Detrended Price Oscillator (DPO)</strong> is a momentum oscillator that helps traders identify short-term cycles or overbought/oversold conditions in a financial asset. It accomplishes this by comparing the current price to a historical average, typically the simple moving average (SMA) of the price over a specified lookback period. By detrending the price data, the DPO filters out longer-term trends, focusing on shorter-term price movements. This allows traders to identify potential reversals or shifts in market sentiment.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="dti" tabindex="-1">dti <a class="header-anchor" href="#dti" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;dti&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">dti(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Directional Trend Index (DTI)</strong> by William Blau is a technical indicator that combines elements of ADX and DMI to gauge both trend strength and direction in the market.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>r</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>s</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>u</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="dx" tabindex="-1">dx <a class="header-anchor" href="#dx" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;dx&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Directional Movement Index (DMI)</strong> is a technical indicator that assesses the strength and direction of a trend in a financial asset.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>di_length</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>adx_smoothing</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>DX(adx, plusDI, minusDI)</p><h2 id="edcf" tabindex="-1">edcf <a class="header-anchor" href="#edcf" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;edcf&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre <strong>Ehlers Distance Coefficient Filter</strong> filters out high-frequency noise from price data while preserving the underlying trend. It calculates the distance between current price and a weighted moving average, adjusting the weighting factor based on market conditions to provide a smoother and more accurate representation of price trends.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=15</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - strength of bulls or bears in the market. It is calculated by multiplying the price change by the volume, providing insights into the underlying force driving the current trend.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=13</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - for <strong>Exponential Moving Average</strong>, which is a type of moving average that places more weight on recent data points, making it more responsive to recent price changes compared to a simple moving average (SMA).</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - Ehlers and Ric Way, decomposes time series signals into intrinsic mode functions (IMFs) and a residual component, revealing underlying cyclical patterns in the <strong>Ease of Movement</strong>, is a technical indicator designed to assess the relationship between price and volume in the market. It quantifies the ease with which prices move by dividing the change in price by the volume, helping traders identify potential trend reversals or continuation patterns based on divergence between price and volume movements.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>length</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>div</code>: int - <strong>End Point Moving Average (EPMA)</strong> is a type of moving average that calculates the average of the most recent data points, emphasizing the endpoint of the data series. It aims to provide a smoother representation of recent price trends while minimizing lag compared to traditional moving averages.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=11</li><li><code>offset</code>: int - <strong>Efficiency Ratio (ER)</strong>, or Kaufman Efficiency Indicator, quantifies the efficiency of price movements by comparing net price change to total price movement over a specified period, FisherTransform</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Fisher Transform</strong> is a technical indicator developed by John Ehlers that transforms prices into a Gaussian distribution to make trends and turning points easier to identify. It converts price data into values that oscillate between -1 and 1, making it particularly useful for detecting trend reversals.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=9</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>FisherTransform(fisher, signal)</p><h2 id="fosc" tabindex="-1">fosc <a class="header-anchor" href="#fosc" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;fosc&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">fosc(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span <strong>Forecast Oscillator (FOSC)</strong> is a technical indicator that measures the difference between the current price and a forecasted price based on a linear regression over a specified period. It helps traders identify potential overbought or oversold conditions and assess the strength of a trend by comparing the actual price to the expected price.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="frama" tabindex="-1">frama <a class="header-anchor" href="#frama" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;frama&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">SC</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span <strong>Fractal Adaptive Moving Average (FRAMA)</strong> is a type of moving average that adjusts its sensitivity to market volatility. It dynamically changes the length of the moving average based on recent price volatility, aiming to provide smoother and more accurate trend signals compared to traditional moving averages.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>window</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>FC</code>: int - default=1</li><li><code>SC</code>: int - default=300</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="fwma" tabindex="-1">fwma <a class="header-anchor" href="#fwma" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;fwma&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span ratios, typically 0.618 and 0.382. This weighting scheme aims to give more importance to recent data while still considering historical prices, providing a smoother trend indicator compared to simple moving averages.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="gatorosc" tabindex="-1">gatorosc <a class="header-anchor" href="#gatorosc" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;gatorosc&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">gatorosc(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> GATOR</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Gator Oscillator</strong>, developed by Bill M. Williams, is a technical indicator used to identify the presence of trends and their relative strength in the market. It consists of two histograms, one representing the difference between the Alligator&#39;s jaw and teeth (blue) and the other representing the difference between the teeth and lips (red). The convergence and divergence of these histograms provide signals for potential changes in trend direction and momentum.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>GATOR(upper, lower, upper_change, lower_change)</p><h2 id="gauss" tabindex="-1">gauss <a class="header-anchor" href="#gauss" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;gauss&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" <strong>Gaussian Filter</strong> is a data filtering technique used to smooth out noise and extract underlying trends or patterns from a signal. It applies a Gaussian distribution or bell-shaped curve to weight data points, giving more emphasis to points closer to the center and less weight to those farther away. This helps in reducing noise while preserving the integrity of the signal.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=14</li><li><code>poles</code>: int - default=4</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="heikin-ashi-candles" tabindex="-1">heikin_ashi_candles <a class="header-anchor" href="#heikin-ashi-candles" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;heikin\_ashi\_candles&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">heikin_ashi_candles(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> HA</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Heikin Ashi candlesticks</strong> are a type of Japanese candlestick charting technique that uses modified candlesticks to filter out market noise and emphasize trends. Each Heikin Ashi candlestick is calculated based on the average prices of the current and previous periods, resulting in smoother candlestick patterns compared to traditional candlesticks. They help traders identify trends more easily and make informed decisions based on trend direction and momentum.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>HA(open, close, high, low)</p><h2 id="high-pass" tabindex="-1">high_pass <a class="header-anchor" href="#high-pass" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;high\_pass&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">high_pass(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">48</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>1-pole High Pass Filter</strong>, by John F. Ehlers, is a digital filter designed to reduce low-frequency noise while retaining high-frequency components in a signal.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=48</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="high-pass-2-pole" tabindex="-1">high_pass_2_pole <a class="header-anchor" href="#high-pass-2-pole" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;high\_pass\_2\_pole&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">high_pass_2_pole(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">48</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>2-pole High Pass Filter</strong>, developed by John F. Ehlers, is a digital filter that attenuates low-frequency components while preserving high-frequency components in a signal. It achieves this by utilizing two poles in its transfer function, offering improved noise reduction compared to a single-pole filter.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=48</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - class="header-anchor" href="#hma" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;hma&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">hma(candles: style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;">&quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Hull Moving Average (HMA)</strong> is a type of moving average developed by Alan Hull that aims to reduce lag while maintaining smoothness. It achieves this by using a weighted average of three different exponential moving averages (EMAs) with different periods. The resulting moving average is more responsive to recent price movements compared to traditional moving averages, making it useful for identifying trends and potential entry or exit points.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="hurst-exponent" tabindex="-1">hurst_exponent <a class="header-anchor" href="#hurst-exponent" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;hurst\_exponent&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">hurst_exponent(candles: np.ndarray, min_chunksize: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 8</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, max_chunksize: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 200</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, num_chunksize: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 5</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, method: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 1</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, source_type: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">str</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;"> &quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> float</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Hurst Exponent</strong> is a statistical measure used to quantify the long-term memory of a time series data. It indicates the degree of self-similarity or fractal nature of the data, helping to identify whether the data is trending, mean-reverting, or displaying random behavior. In simpler terms, the function helps quantify how likely trends in the data will continue. A Hurst exponent close to 0.5 indicates random fluctuations, while values closer to 1 suggest persistent trends. The function offers different methods for this estimation and allows you to choose the most suitable one for your data.</p><p>#trend</p><div class="tip custom-block"><p class="custom-block-title">methods</p><ul><li>RS: Estimates the Hurst (H) exponent using the R/S method from the time series. The R/S method consists of dividing the series into pieces of equal size <code>series_len</code> and calculating the rescaled range. This repeats the process for several <code>series_len</code> values and adjusts data regression to obtain the H. <code>series_len</code> will take values between <code>min_chunksize</code> and <code>max_chunksize</code>, the step size from <code>min_chunksize</code> to <code>max_chunksize</code> can be controlled through the parameter <code>step_chunksize</code>.</li><li>DMA: Estimates the Hurst (H) exponent using the DMA method from the time series. The DMA method consists on calculate the moving average of size <code>series_len</code> and subtract it to the original series and calculating the standard deviation of that result. This repeats the process for several <code>series_len</code>values and adjusts data regression to obtain the H. <code>series_len</code> will take values between <code>min_chunksize</code> and <code>max_chunksize</code>, the step size from<code>min_chunksize</code> to <code>max_chunksize</code> can be controlled through the parameter<code>step_chunksize</code>.</li><li>DSOD: The estimation is based on the discrete second order derivative. Consists on get two different noise of the original series and calculate the standard deviation and calculate the slope of two point with that values.</li></ul></div><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>min_chunksize</code>: int - default=8</li><li><code>max_chunksize</code>: int - default=200</li><li><code>num_chunksize</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>method</code>: int - default=1 - 0: RS | 1: DMA | 2: DSOD</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float</p><h2 id="hwma" tabindex="-1">hwma <a class="header-anchor" href="#hwma" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;hwma&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light &quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, sequential: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">bool</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Holt-Winters Moving Average</strong>, also known as the Triple Exponential Smoothing, is a method used for forecasting time series data. It extends the Exponential Moving Average (EMA) by incorporating seasonal components, making it suitable for capturing and predicting seasonal patterns in data.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>na</code>: float - default=0.2</li><li><code>nb</code>: float - default=0.1</li><li><code>nc</code>: float - default=0.1</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="ichimoku-cloud" tabindex="-1">ichimoku_cloud <a class="header-anchor" href="#ichimoku-cloud" exiting trades based on the sequence of signals generated by the Ichimoku components. It aims to capture trends and reversals in the market by providing clear guidelines for trade execution, often incorporating criteria such as the alignment of different Ichimoku lines and the positioning of price relative to the Cloud.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>conversion_line_period</code>: int - &quot;jsa&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">jsa(candles: np.ndarray, period: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 30</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, source_type: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">str</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;"> &quot;close&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, sequential: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">bool</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Jsa Moving Average</strong> computes the midpoint of a given price series by averaging each element with the element shifted forward by a specified period.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=30</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="kama" tabindex="-1">kama <a class="header-anchor" href="#kama" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kama&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">kama(candles: style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Kaufman Adaptive Moving Average (KAMA)</strong> is a type of moving average developed by Perry Kaufman. It dynamically adjusts its smoothing period based on market volatility, aiming to provide a more accurate representation of price trends while minimizing lag. KAMA increases its responsiveness during periods of high volatility and decreases it during periods of low volatility, making it particularly useful in adapting to changing market conditions.</p><p>#trend</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=30</li><li><code>fast_length</code>: int - default=2</li><li><code>slow_length</code>: int - default=30</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="kaufmanstop" tabindex="-1">kaufmanstop <a class="header-anchor" href="#kaufmanstop" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kaufmanstop&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">kaufmanstop(candles: np.ndarray, period: </span><span </span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Perry Kaufman&#39;s Stops</strong> are dynamic exit strategy indicators that provide adaptive stop-loss levels that adjust based on market conditions, aiming to protect profits and limit losses effectively.</p><p>#exit</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=22</li><li><code>mult</code>: float - default=2</li><li><code>direction</code>: str - default=&quot;long&quot; | &quot;short&quot;</li><li><code>matype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="kdj" tabindex="-1">kdj <a class="header-anchor" href="#kdj" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kdj&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">kdj(candles: np.ndarray, fastk_period: </span><span slowk_matype: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span 3</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, slowd_matype: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">bool</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> KDJ</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>KDJ Oscillator</strong> is derived from the Stochastic Oscillator. It consists of three lines: %K, %D, and the J line. The %K line compares the current closing price to the recent trading range, while the %D line is a moving average of %K. The J line represents the difference between %D and a smoothed %D. The KDJ Oscillator helps traders identify overbought and oversold conditions and potential trend reversals.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>fastk_period</code>: int - default=9</li><li><code>slowk_period</code>: int - default=3</li><li><code>slowk_matype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>slowd_period</code>: int - default=3</li><li><code>slowd_matype</code>: int - default=0</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>KDJ(k, d, j)</p><h2 id="keltner" tabindex="-1">keltner <a class="header-anchor" href="#keltner" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;keltner&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">source_type</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> KeltnerChannel</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Keltner Channels</strong> are volatility-based technical indicators used to identify potential price breakouts and trend reversals in the market. They consist of three lines: the middle line, which is typically a moving average of the asset&#39;s price, and an upper and lower channel line, which are derived from the middle line by adding and subtracting a multiple of the Average True Range (ATR). Keltner Channels expand and contract based on market volatility, providing traders with a visual representation of price volatility and potential support and resistance levels.</p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>multiplier</code>: float - default=2</li><li><code>matype</code>: int - default=1</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>KeltnerChannel(upperband, middleband, lowerband)</p><h2 id="kst" tabindex="-1">kst <a class="header-anchor" href="#kst" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kst&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light KST</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">:</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Know Sure Thing (KST)</strong> is a momentum oscillator developed by Martin Pring. It combines multiple smoothed rate-of-change indicators over different periods to generate a single composite momentum indicator. The KST aims to identify significant trend changes and overbought or oversold conditions in the market.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>sma_period1</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>sma_period2</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>sma_period3</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>sma_period4</code>: int - default=15</li><li><code>roc_period1</code>: int - default=10</li><li><code>roc_period2</code>: int - default=15</li><li><code>roc_period3</code>: int - default=20</li><li><code>roc_period4</code>: int - default=30</li><li><code>signal_period</code>: int - default=9</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;close&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>KST(line, signal)</p><h2 id="kurtosis" tabindex="-1">kurtosis <a class="header-anchor" href="#kurtosis" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kurtosis&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">kurtosis(candles: np.ndarray, period: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">int</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> 5</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, source_type: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">str</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#032F62;--shiki-dark:#9ECBFF;"> &quot;hl2&quot;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, sequential: </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">bool</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;"> =</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;"> False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p><strong>Kurtosis</strong> is a statistical measure used to quantify the &quot;tailedness&quot; or &quot;peakedness&quot; of a probability distribution. It provides insights into the shape of the distribution of returns for a given asset. Positive kurtosis indicates a distribution with heavier tails and a more peaked shape than the normal distribution, while negative kurtosis indicates lighter tails and a flatter shape.</p><p>#volatility</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>period</code>: int - default=5</li><li><code>source_type</code>: str - default=&quot;hl2&quot;</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="kvo" tabindex="-1">kvo <a class="header-anchor" href="#kvo" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;kvo&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span class="lang">python</span><pre class="shiki shiki-themes github-light github-dark vp-code" tabindex="0"><code><span class="line"><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">kvo(candles: np.ndarray, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">short_period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">34</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">long_period</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">55</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, </span><span style="--shiki-light:#E36209;--shiki-dark:#FFAB70;">sequential</span><span style="--shiki-light:#D73A49;--shiki-dark:#F97583;">=</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">False</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">) </span><span style="--shiki-light:#B31D28;--shiki-light-font-style:italic;--shiki-dark:#FDAEB7;--shiki-dark-font-style:italic;">-&gt;</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;"> Union[</span><span style="--shiki-light:#005CC5;--shiki-dark:#79B8FF;">float</span><span style="--shiki-light:#24292E;--shiki-dark:#E1E4E8;">, np.ndarray]</span></span></code></pre></div><p>The <strong>Klinger Volume Oscillator (KVO)</strong> is a volume-based technical indicator developed by Stephen J. Klinger. It combines two volume-based moving averages—the volume force and the volume trend—to identify bullish and bearish trends in the market. The KVO helps traders assess the relationship between price and volume, providing insights into potential trend reversals or continuations.</p><p>#momentum</p><p><strong>Arguments</strong>:</p><ul><li><code>candles</code>: np.ndarray</li><li><code>short_period</code>: int - default=34</li><li><code>long_period</code>: int - default=55</li><li><code>sequential</code>: bool - default=False</li></ul><p><strong>Returns</strong>:</p><p>float | np.ndarray</p><h2 id="linearreg" tabindex="-1">linearreg <a class="header-anchor" href="#linearreg" aria-label="Permalink to &quot;linearreg&quot;">​</a></h2><div class="language-python vp-adaptive-theme"><button title="Copy Code" class="copy"></button><span
